In the opinion of Modrall, Sperling, Roehl, Harris & Sisk, P.A., Bond Counsel, under existing laws, regulations, rulings and judicial
decisions, and assuming compliance with certain covenants described in “TAX EXEMPTION” herein, interest on the 2019 Bonds (a) is
excludable from the gross income of the recipients thereof for federal income tax purposes under Section 103 of the Internal Revenue Code, as
amended; and (b) is not an item of tax preference under Section 57 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended, for purposes of the
federal alternative minimum tax imposed on individuals. Bond Counsel is also of the opinion, based on existing laws of the State of New Mexico
as enacted and construed, that the 2019 Bonds and income from the 2019 Bonds are exempt from all taxation by the State of New Mexico or any
political subdivision thereof. For a more complete description of such opinion of Bond Counsel and a description of certain provisions of the
Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended, which may affect the federal tax treatment of interest on the 2019 Bonds for certain registered
owners of such bonds, see “TAX EXEMPTION” herein.

City of Santa Fe, New Mexico
Net Wastewater Utility System / Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Improvement
Revenue Bonds
Series 2019
(Climate Bond Certified / Green Bonds)
Dated: Date of Delivery Due: June 1, as shown on the inside front cover
The $13,550,000 City of Santa Fe, New Mexico Net Wastewater Utility System / Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax
Improvement Revenue Bonds, Series 2019 (the “2019 Bonds” or the “Bonds”) are being issued by the City of Santa Fe, New Mexico (the “City”)
to provide funds for the Improvement Project (as defined herein). See “SOURCES AND USES OF FUNDS” herein. The 2019 Bonds will bear
interest from the date of delivery, at the rates set forth on the inside front cover hereof, payable semiannually on June 1 and December 1 of each
year until maturity, commencing June 1, 2019, and will mature on June 1 of each of the years as set forth on the inside front cover hereof.
The 2019 Bonds are issuable as fully registered bonds in denominations of $5,000 or any integral multiple thereof. The 2019 Bonds
will be issued pursuant to a book-entry only system and will be registered in the name of Cede & Co., as nominee of The Depository Trust
Company, New York, New York (“DTC”). Purchasers of the 2019 Bonds (“Beneficial Owners”) will not receive physical delivery of bond
certificates representing their beneficial ownership interests. So long as DTC or its nominee is the owner of the 2019 Bonds, principal of and
interest on the 2019 Bonds will be paid by the Paying Agent (as defined herein) to DTC or its nominee, which will in turn remit such payment to
its Direct Participants (as defined herein) for subsequent disbursement by the Direct Participants and the Indirect Participants (as defined herein)
to the Beneficial Owners. See “DESCRIPTION OF THE 2019 BONDS—Book-Entry Only System.”
The 2019 Bonds, together with the interest accruing thereon, will be payable solely from a first lien, but not an exclusive first lien on
Net Revenues and a subordinate lien, but not an exclusive subordinate lien, on the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues as
described and defined herein (collectively, the “Pledged Revenues”). Net Revenues consist of all income and revenues directly or indirectly
derived by the City from the operation and use of the municipally owned public utility designated as the City’s wastewater utility system (the
“Wastewater Utility System”, the “System” or the “Wastewater System”) or any part of the Wastewater Utility System, less Wastewater Utility
System Operation and Maintenance Expenses (as defined herein). The lien on the Pledged Revenues will be on parity with the lien on the
Pledged Revenues securing any Parity Obligations (as defined herein).
The 2019 Bonds are subject to optional redemption prior to maturity as more fully described herein. See “DESCRIPTION OF THE
2019 BONDS—Redemption of 2019 Bonds” herein.
The registered owners of the 2019 Bonds may not look to any general or other fund of the City for the payment of the principal of and
interest on the 2019 Bonds except for the Pledged Revenues. The 2019 Bonds do not constitute an indebtedness of the City within the meaning
of any constitutional, charter or statutory provision or limitation, nor will they be considered or held to be general obligations of the City.
Neither the full faith and credit of the City nor the taxing power of the City, the State or any political subdivision or public agency thereof, other
than the City to the extent of the Pledged Revenues, are pledged to the payment of the principal of and interest on the 2019 Bonds. No Owner
has the right to compel the exercise of the taxing power of the City or the forfeiture of any of its property in connection with any default under
the Bond Ordinance (as defined herein).
The purchase and ownership of the 2019 Bonds involve investment risk and may not be suitable for all investors. This cover page is
not intended to be a summary of the terms of, or the security for, the 2019 Bonds. Investors are advised to read this Official Statement in its
entirety to obtain information essential to the making of an informed investment decision.
The 2019 Bonds are offered when, as and if issued and received by the underwriters set forth below (the “Underwriters”) subject to the
approval of validity by Modrall, Sperling, Roehl, Harris & Sisk, P.A., Albuquerque, New Mexico, Bond Counsel. Modrall, Sperling, Roehl,
Harris & Sisk, P.A., has also acted as special counsel to the City in connection with the preparation of this Official Statement. Certain legal
matters will be passed on for the City by Erin K. McSherry, City Attorney. Certain legal matters will passed upon for the Underwriters by
McCall, Parkhurst & Horton L.L.P., Dallas, Texas. It is anticipated that the 2019 Bonds will be available for delivery through the facilities of
DTC on or about March 20, 2019.
Dated: February 27, 2019

CITY OF SANTA FE, NEW MEXICO
NET WASTEWATER UTILITY SYSTEM / ENVIRONMENTAL SERVICES GROSS
RECEIPTS TAX IMPROVEMENT REVENUE BONDS
SERIES 2019
(CLIMATE BOND CERTIFIED / GREEN BONDS)
SUMMARY OF INFORMATION
There follows a summary of certain provisions discussed in this Official Statement. SUCH
SUMMARY DOES NOT PURPORT TO BE COMPREHENSIVE OR DEFINITIVE AND IS
QUALIFIED IN ITS ENTIRETY BY REFERENCE TO THE COMPLETE OFFICIAL STATEMENT.
This Summary is only a brief statement and a full review of the entire Official Statement should be made
by potential investors. Capitalized terms used but not otherwise defined in this “SUMMARY OF
INFORMATION” will have the meanings given such terms in “APPENDIX C—DEFINITIONS OF
CERTAIN TERMS.”
Dated: Date of delivery.
Registration: The City of Santa Fe, New Mexico Net Wastewater Utility System /
Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Improvement Revenue
Bonds, Series 2019 (the “2019 Bonds” or the “Bonds”) will be issued as
fully registered bonds in denominations of $5,000 and integral multiples
thereof. The Registrar is BOKF, NA.
Principal Payment: The 2019 Bonds will mature on June 1 of each of the years set forth on
the inside front cover page of this Official Statement.
Interest Payment: Interest will be payable semiannually on June 1 and December 1,
commencing on June 1, 2019.
Security: The 2019 Bonds are special limited obligations, payable solely from the
Pledged Revenues. The Pledged Revenues consist of a first lien, but not
an exclusive first lien, on the Net Revenues and a subordinate lien, but
not an exclusive subordinate lien, on Pledged Environmental Services
Gross Receipts Tax Revenues. Net Revenues are defined as all income
and revenues directly or indirectly derived by the City from the operation
and use of the municipally owned public utility designated as the City’s
wastewater utility system (the “Wastewater Utility System”) or any part
of the Wastewater Utility System, less Wastewater Utility System
Operation and Maintenance Expenses. The Environmental Services
Gross Receipts Tax Revenues are derived from the Environmental
Services Gross Receipts Tax imposed pursuant to Section 7-19D-10
NMSA 1978 and City Ordinance No. 1993-20 on persons engaging in
business in the City in the amount of 1/16 th of one percent of the gross
receipts of such persons. See “SECURITY AND SOURCES OF
PAYMENT FOR THE 2019 BONDS” herein.
Reserve Account: At the time of issuance of the 2019 Bonds, a portion of the proceeds of
the 2019 Bonds will be utilized to purchase a reserve fund insurance
policy with coverage in the amount of the Reserve Requirement (defined
herein) which is $1,190,800.00.iv
Parity Obligations: The 2019 Bonds, when issued, will be payable from the Pledged
Revenues on parity with the City’s Gross Receipts Tax (Subordinate
Lien)/Wastewater System Refunding Revenue Bonds, Series 2012B (the
“2012B Bonds”) and any other Parity Obligations issued subsequent to
the issuance of the 2019 Bonds, as more fully described herein. See
“SECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT FOR THE 2019
BONDS” herein.
Special Obligations: THE 2019 BONDS ARE SPECIAL LIMITED OBLIGATIONS,
PAYABLE SOLELY FROM PLEDGED REVENUES. THE
PRINCIPAL OF AND INTEREST ON THE 2019 BONDS WILL BE
PAYABLE FROM PLEDGED REVENUES, AND WILL NOT BE
PAYABLE FROM ANY FUNDS OF THE CITY EXCEPT THE
DESIGNATED SPECIAL FUNDS PLEDGED TO THE PAYMENT OF
THE 2019 BONDS. THE 2019 BONDS DO NOT CONSTITUTE AN
INDEBTEDNESS OF THE CITY WITHIN THE MEANING OF ANY
CONSTITUTIONAL, CHARTER OR STATUTORY PROVISION OR
LIMITATION, NOR WILL THEY BE CONSIDERED OR HELD TO
BE GENERAL OBLIGATIONS OF THE CITY. NEITHER THE FULL
FAITH AND CREDIT NOR THE TAXING POWER OF THE CITY,
THE STATE OR ANY POLITICAL SUBDIVISION OR PUBLIC
AGENCY THEREOF, OTHER THAN THE CITY TO THE EXTENT
OF THE PLEDGED REVENUES, ARE PLEDGED TO THE
PAYMENT OF THE PRINCIPAL OF AND INTEREST ON THE 2019
BONDS. NO OWNER HAS THE RIGHT TO COMPEL THE
EXERCISE OF THE TAXING POWER OF THE CITY OR THE
FORFEITURE OF ANY OF ITS PROPERTY IN CONNECTION
WITH ANY DEFAULT UNDER THE BOND ORDINANCE.
Wastewater Utility System: The Wastewater Utility System consists of the municipally owned public
utility designated as the City’s wastewater utility system consisting of all
properties, real, personal, mixed or otherwise, now owned or hereafter
acquired by the City through purchase, construction or otherwise,
including any expansions, extensions, enlargements and improvements
of or to the Wastewater Utility System, and used in connection therewith
or relating thereto, and any other related activity or enterprise of the City
designated by the Council as part of the Wastewater Utility System,
whether situated within or without the limits of the City.
Rate Covenant: Pursuant to the Bond Ordinance, the City has covenanted that it will at
all times fix rates and collect charges for each class of service rendered
by the Wastewater System, and to, from time to time, amend or adjust
such rates to fix, charge and collect such rates and charges so that
Wastewater System Gross Revenues, together with the Environmental
Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues, shall always be sufficient to
provide for the payment of the Debt Service Requirements on all
Outstanding Parity Obligations and subordinate Obligations as and when
the same become due and payable, to maintain the funds and accounts
established in the Ordinance, to provide for the payment of Wastewater
System Operation and Maintenance Expenses which may be necessary to
preserve the same in good repair and working order, including thev
necessary reserves therefor and all other payments necessary to meet on-
going legal obligations to be paid at that time; and
The City further covenants that it will at all times fix, charge and collect
such rates and charges as shall be required in order that in each Fiscal
Year the Wastewater System Net Revenues, together with the
Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues, shall at least
equal the greater of (a) the Debt Service Requirements on all
Outstanding Parity Obligations and subordinate Obligations in such
Fiscal Year and the deposits required by the Ordinance to be made into
the various funds of the Ordinance in such year or (b) 110% of the Debt
Service Requirements on all Outstanding Parity Obligations and
Subordinate Obligations in such Fiscal Year. See “SUMMARY OF
CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF THE BOND ORDINANCE— Protective
Covenants of the City” herein.
Prior Redemption: The 2019 Bonds maturing on or after June 1, 2029 are subject to
redemption prior to maturity at the option of the City, in whole or in part,
on June 1, 2028 and any date thereafter at par, plus accrued interest to the
redemption date, without premium. See “DESCRIPTION OF THE 2019
BONDS—Redemption of 2019 Bonds” herein.
Additional Bonds: Additional obligations may hereafter be issued which are secured by and
payable from the Pledged Revenues on parity with the 2019 Bonds.
Additional obligations may hereafter be issued and secured by the
Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues. See
“SUMMARY OF CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF THE BOND
ORDINANCE—Additional Bonds and Other Obligations” herein.
Additional Superior Tax Obligations with a lien on the Environmental
Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues superior to the lien thereon of the
2019 Bonds may be issued so long as the Additional Gross Receipts Tax
Revenues (as defined herein) are also pledged to the Obligations. The
State Shared Gross Receipts Tax Revenues, One-Half Percent Municipal
Gross Receipts Tax Revenues and the Infrastructure Gross Receipts Tax
Revenues (collectively, the “Additional Gross Receipts Tax Revenues”)
are not pledged to the payment of the 2019 Bonds. There are currently
no Superior Tax Obligations outstanding.
Purpose: The 2019 Bonds are being issued to provide funds for extending,
enlarging, bettering, repairing and otherwise improving the System and
paying the costs of issuance of the 2019 Bonds. See “THE
IMPROVEMENT PROJECT”, “SOURCES AND USES OF FUNDS”,
and “CLIMATE BOND CERTIFICATION” herein.
Climate Bonds Initiative: The City has designated the 2019 Bonds as “Climate Bond Certified /
Green Bonds” and the Climate Bonds Initiative has provided a
certification to the City of the 2019 Bonds as “Certified Climate Bonds.”
See “CLIMATE BOND CERTIFICATION” herein.
Bond Counsel: Modrall, Sperling, Roehl, Harris & Sisk, P.A., Albuquerque, New
Mexico.vi
Financial Advisor: Hilltop Securities Inc., Dallas, Texas
Paying Agent/Registrar: BOKF, NA, Albuquerque, New Mexico,
Underwriters: RBC Capital Markets, LLC and Piper Jaffray & Co.
Special Factors: Investors and prospective investors should give particular attention to
various factors, including that the 2019 Bonds are limited obligations and
that additional obligations may be issued and secured by and paid from
the Pledged Revenues. See “SPECIAL FACTORS RELATING TO
THE 2019 BONDS”, “SECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT
FOR THE 2019 BONDS — Pledged Net Revenues”, “SECURITY AND
SOURCES OF PAYMENT FOR THE 2019 BONDS — Pledged
Environmental Gross Receipts Tax Revenues” and “SUMMARY OF
CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF THE BOND ORDINANCE—Additional
Obligations” herein.1

INTRODUCTION
This Official Statement, which includes the cover page and the appendices hereto, sets forth
certain information in connection with the offering of $13,550,000 aggregate principal amount of City of
Santa Fe, New Mexico, Net Wastewater Utility System / Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax
Improvement Revenue Bonds, Series 2019 (the “2019 Bonds”) to be issued by the City of Santa Fe,
Santa Fe County, New Mexico (the “City,” the “County” and the “State,” respectively), pursuant to
Ordinance No. 2019-02, adopted on January 30, 2019 (the “Bond Ordinance”) and the Pricing Certificate
executed on February 27, 2019.
The 2019 Bonds are payable solely from a first lien (but not an exclusive first lien) on the Net
Revenues and a subordinate lien (but not an exclusive subordinate lien) on the Environmental Services
Gross Receipts Tax Revenues (both as defined herein and collectively referred to as the Pledged
Revenues) on parity with the lien thereon of the 2012B Bonds. The Net Revenues consist of all income
and revenues directly or indirectly derived by the City from the operation and use of the municipally
owned public utility designated as the City’s wastewater utility system (the “Wastewater Utility System”)
or any part of the Wastewater Utility System, less Wastewater Utility System Operation and Maintenance
Expenses (as defined herein). The Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues consist of the
revenues derived from the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax imposed pursuant to Section 7-
19D-10 NMSA 1978 and City Ordinance No. 1993-20 on persons engaging in business in the City in the
amount of 1/16th of one percent of the gross receipts of such persons. The 2019 Bonds are special, limited
obligations of the City payable from and secured solely by the Pledged Revenues. See “SECURITY
AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT FOR THE 2019 BONDS” herein.
The City has previously issued its 2012B Bonds in an aggregate principal amount of $14,280,000,
of which, $4,955,000 is currently outstanding which is secured by a lien on the Pledged Revenues on
parity with the lien of the 2019 Bonds. The 2012B Bonds are also secured by a subordinate lien on
certain Additional Gross Receipts Tax Revenues of the City which are not pledged to the 2019 Bonds.
The 2019 Bonds are secured and payable from a lien on the Pledged Revenues on parity with the
lien of the 2012B Bonds. In addition to the 2012B Bonds, and the 2019 Bonds, additional bonds may be
issued and secured by the Pledged Revenues having a lien on the Pledged Revenues on parity with the
lien on the Pledged Revenues securing the 2012B Bonds and the 2019 Bonds. The 2012B Bonds, the
2019 Bonds, and any additional bonds that may be issued and secured by the Pledged Revenues having a
lien on the Pledged Revenues on parity with the lien on the Pledged Revenues securing the 2012B Bonds
and the 2019 Bonds are collectively referred to herein as “Parity Obligations.” The City may issue
Superior Tax Obligations payable, in part, from the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax
Revenues with a lien thereon superior to the lien of the 2019 Bonds so long as the City pledges the
Additional Gross Receipts Tax Revenues in conjunction with the issuance of the additional Superior Tax
Obligations. The Additional Gross Receipts Tax Revenues are not pledged to the payment of the 2019
Bonds. There are currently no outstanding Superior Tax Obligations. See “SUMMARY OF CERTAIN
PROVISIONS OF THE BOND ORDINANCE—Additional Bonds and Other Obligations.”2

FUNDS OF THE CITY EXCEPT THE DESIGNATED SPECIAL FUNDS PLEDGED TO THE

OR HELD TO BE GENERAL OBLIGATIONS OF THE CITY. NEITHER THE FULL FAITH AND

SUBDIVISION OR PUBLIC AGENCY THEREOF, OTHER THAN THE CITY TO THE EXTENT OF
THE PLEDGED REVENUES, ARE PLEDGED TO THE PAYMENT OF THE PRINCIPAL OF AND
INTEREST ON THE 2019 BONDS. NO OWNER HAS THE RIGHT TO COMPEL THE EXERCISE
OF THE TAXING POWER OF THE CITY OR THE FORFEITURE OF ANY OF ITS PROPERTY IN

SPECIAL FACTORS RELATING TO THE 2019 BONDS
Each prospective investor of the 2019 Bonds is encouraged to read this Official Statement and to
give particular attention to the factors described below which, among other conditions, could affect the
payment of debt service on the 2019 Bonds and could affect the market price of the 2019 Bonds to an
extent that cannot be determined at this time.
Limited Obligations
The 2019 Bonds are limited obligations of the City payable as to principal and interest solely
from Pledged Revenues. Therefore, the security for the punctual payment of the principal of and interest
on the 2019 Bonds is dependent on the City’s receipt of the Pledged Revenues in an amount sufficient to
meet the debt service requirements of the 2019 Bonds and the Parity Obligations. See “SECURITY AND
SOURCES OF PAYMENT FOR THE 2019 BONDS,” “INFORMATION CONCERNING
ENVIRONMENTAL SERVICES GROSS RECEIPTS TAX AND REVENUES” and “THE
WASTEWATER UTILITY SYSTEM” herein. The 2019 Bonds and the interest thereon do not constitute
a debt or indebtedness of the City within the meaning of any provision or limitation of the Constitution or
laws of the State and do not give rise to a pecuniary liability of the City or a charge against its general
credit or taxing power. Further, the 2019 Bonds are not obligations of the State, and the owners of the
2019 Bonds may not look to the State for payment of the principal of or interest on the 2019 Bonds.
NEITHER THE FULL FAITH AND CREDIT NOR THE TAXING POWER OF THE CITY,
THE STATE OR ANY POLITICAL SUBDIVISION OR PUBLIC AGENCY THEREOF, OTHER
THAN THE CITY TO THE EXTENT OF THE PLEDGED REVENUES, ARE PLEDGED TO THE
PAYMENT OF THE PRINCIPAL OF AND INTEREST ON THE 2019 BONDS.
Additional Obligations Payable From Pledged Revenues
The issuance of Obligations with a superior lien on the Net Revenues is prohibited under the
Bond Ordinance. Additional Obligations may be issued with a lien on the Net Revenues and3
Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues on parity with the lien thereon of the 2019 Bonds
in accordance with the requirements of the Bond Ordinance. Additional Superior Tax Obligations may be
issued in accordance with the provisions of the Bond Ordinance so long as the Additional Gross Receipts
Tax Revenues are pledged to the payment of Superior Tax Obligations. There are currently no
outstanding Superior Tax Obligations. See “SUMMARY OF CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF THE BOND
ORDINANCE—Additional Bonds and Other Obligations.”
Compliance with Rate Covenant
Pursuant to the Bond Ordinance, the City has covenanted to fix, charge and collect such rates and
charges as shall be required in order that in each Fiscal Year the Wastewater System Net Revenues,
together with the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues, shall at least equal the greater of
(a) the Debt Service Requirements on all Outstanding Parity Obligations and Obligations with a lien on
the Pledged Revenues subordinate to the lien thereon of the 2019 Bonds and the 2012B Bonds (the
“Subordinate Obligations”) in such Fiscal Year and the deposits required by the Ordinance to be made
into the various funds of the Ordinance in such year or (b) 110% of the Debt Service Requirements on all
Outstanding Parity Obligations and Subordinate Obligations in such Fiscal Year. See “SUMMARY OF
CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF THE BOND ORDINANCE—Protective Covenants of the City” herein.
Gross Receipts Tax Collections are Subject to Fluctuation; Effect of Tourism
Gross receipts tax collections are subject to the fluctuations in spending related, in part, to
national and local economic conditions, which determine the amount of gross receipts taxes collected.
This causes gross receipts tax revenues to increase along with the increasing prices brought about by
inflation, but also causes collections to be vulnerable to adverse economic conditions and reduced
spending. The City’s economic base and the future collections of Environmental Services Gross Receipts
Tax Revenues are impacted by tourism and summer and winter resort activities. The City’s associated
retail sales are affected by both weather and general economic circumstances.
The Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues are based on the total gross receipts of
persons transacting business within the City that is subject to payment of the gross receipts taxes that
produce Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues. Various circumstances and
developments, most of which are beyond the control of the City, may have an adverse effect on the future
level of Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues. Such circumstances may include, among
others, adverse changes in national and local economic and financial conditions generally, reductions in
the rates of employment and economic growth in the City, the State and the region, a decrease in rates of
population growth and rates of residential and commercial development in the City, the County, the State,
and the region and various other factors.
For the fiscal year ended June 30, 2018, Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues
totaled $2,231,738, representing an increase of 7.49% from the previous fiscal year. Since 2011,
Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues have increased each year. See “INFORMATION
CONCERNING ENVIRONMENTAL SERVICES GROSS RECEIPTS TAXES AND REVENUES”
herein. Additional revenues related to Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues are included
in the percentages described above. The City cannot predict with certainty the future growth or decline of
gross receipts tax revenues. A decline of gross receipts tax revenues may adversely affect the financial
well-being of the City and the City’s ability to make payments on the 2019 Bonds.4
Legislative Changes
Revisions to laws of the State affecting taxed activities and distributions of gross receipts tax
revenues could be adopted in the future by the State Legislature. Proposals affecting taxed activities and
distributions are frequently considered by the State Legislature. There is no assurance that any future
revisions to State laws will not adversely affect activities now subject to the gross receipts tax or
distribution of gross receipts tax revenues to the City. Notwithstanding the foregoing, the provisions of
State law authorizing the issuance of revenue bonds (including bonds secured by gross receipts tax
revenues, such as the 2019 Bonds) include a provision stating that any law which authorizes the pledge of
revenues to the payment of revenue bonds, or which affects the pledged revenue “shall not be repealed or
amended or otherwise directly or indirectly modified in such a manner as to impair adversely any such
outstanding revenue bonds.”
In the 2004 Legislative Session, a bill was adopted by the Legislature and signed into law that
relieved from gross receipts taxes (i) food or food products for home consumption sold at an
establishment that sells food for home preparation and consumption and (ii) receipts from payments by a
managed health care provider or health care insurer for commercial contract services or Medicare Part C
services provided by a health care provider. See Sections 7-9-92 and 7-9-93 NMSA 1978. The law also
provides, pursuant to Section 7-1-6.46 NMSA 1978, for distribution from the State general fund to
municipalities to offset any reduced gross receipts tax distributions resulting from the food and health
care services tax relief effected by Sections 7-9-92 and 7-9-93. A portion of such offset distributions are
included in the Pledged Revenues. However, as discussed below, these distributions began to be reduced
by a legislatively set percentage each year starting in Fiscal Year 2016 and will be phased out entirely by
Fiscal Year 2030.
In the 2012 Legislative session, the State Legislature amended the State Gross Receipts and
Compensating Tax Act as related to certain manufacturing and construction gross receipts. Specifically,
the amendment expanded the gross receipts tax deductions for sales of tangible property to manufacturers
to include property consumed in the process of manufacturing, excluding tools and equipment.
Additionally, the definition of “construction services” was expanded thereby increasing the scope of the
deduction for sale of construction services to persons engaged in the construction business. Both of these
amendments are phased in over the next several fiscal years.
In the 2013 New Mexico Legislative session, House Bill 641, passed by both chambers and
signed by the Governor, included several changes to New Mexico’s tax code. The bill lowers the New
Mexico’s top corporate income tax over five years and permits single sales factor apportioning for certain
manufacturing corporations phased in over five years, amends the gross receipts tax deduction for
tangible property consumed in the manufacturing process, and amends the high-wage jobs tax credit to
extend the credit and add qualifications criteria for the credit. The bill also requires combined reporting
for certain corporations and phases out the hold-harmless distribution to municipalities and counties that
offset the food and medical deductions over 15 years starting in Fiscal Year 2016.
Other amendments to State laws affecting taxed activities and distribution of gross receipts tax
revenues have been proposed from time to time and could be proposed in the future by the Legislature.
There is no assurance that any future amendments will not adversely affect activities now subject to the
gross receipts tax or distribution of gross receipts tax revenues to the City.
The law as currently enacted will result in annual reductions and ultimately the elimination of the
hold harmless distributions to the City, which began on July 1, 2015, as follows:5

In order to offset the reduced hold harmless distributions, the law allows municipalities and
counties to impose a local option gross receipts tax of up to three-eighths of one percent (3/8%) (the
“Hold Harmless Gross Receipts Tax”). The City has not imposed any increment of the Hold Harmless
Gross Receipts Tax and the imposition of any increment of such tax would not be pledged toward
repayment of the 2019 Bonds without additional action by the City Council. It is possible that the New
Mexico Legislature will further amend the law to provide for additional decreases in hold harmless
distributions in the event that a municipality or county imposes any increment of the Hold Harmless
Gross Receipts Tax.
Bankruptcy and Foreclosure
The ability of the State to collect gross receipts taxes owed from an owner or operator of a
business may be adversely affected by the filing of a bankruptcy proceeding by the owner. The ability to
collect delinquent gross receipts taxes using foreclosure and sale for non-payment of taxes may be
forestalled or delayed by bankruptcy, reorganization, insolvency or other similar proceedings affecting the
owner or operator of a business. The Federal bankruptcy laws provide for an automatic stay of
foreclosure and sale proceedings, thereby delaying such proceedings, perhaps for an extended period.
Delays in the exercise of remedies could result in gross receipts tax collections that may be insufficient to
pay debt service on the 2019 Bonds when due.
Secondary Market
No guarantee can be made that a secondary market for the 2019 Bonds will be established and
maintained. Owners of 2019 Bonds should be prepared to hold their bonds to maturity.
Bond Ratings
There is no assurance that the ratings assigned to the 2019 Bonds will not be lowered or
withdrawn at any time, the effect of which could adversely affect the market price or the marketability of
the 2019 Bonds. See the information herein under the caption “RATINGS.”6
THE IMPROVEMENT PROJECT
The 2019 Bonds are being issued in order to provide funds for the Improvement Project. The
Improvement Project consists of extending, enlarging, bettering, repairing and otherwise improving the
Wastewater Utility System and paying all costs incidental thereto and paying the costs of issuance of the
2019 Bonds. Issuance of the 2019 Bonds is expected to provide approximately $15,000,000 in proceeds
to be deposited into the Acquisition Fund for the Improvement Project in addition to amounts required to
pay the costs of issuance of the 2019 Bonds and to acquire a Reserve Fund Insurance Policy for the 2019
Reserve Fund.
The Improvement Project includes constructing two new anaerobic digesters, installing a new
automated control system, adding a third belt filter press for sludge dewatering, and constructing a
cogeneration facility that will utilize the digester-produced biogas as a source of energy. The
Improvement Project is the largest construction project at the City’s Paseo Real Wastewater Treatment
Facility and is part of the 2017/2018 Wastewater Management Five-Year Capital Improvement Plan.
Digesters - The City employs anaerobic digestion for the treatment of municipal wastewater
sludge. The process employs anaerobic digesters to break down organic matter into carbon dioxide and
methane. A portion is converted into gases while the remainder is dried and becomes residual biosolids
that are soil-like material. The City currently has two digesters that were built in 1962 and are
constructed of concrete. The new units will be slightly larger, giving the City additional capacity and
ensuring that they will produce high-quality sludge for land disposal and composting. The new
equipment will employ current technology that will be more efficient than the existing digesters. In a
future project, the existing digesters will be inspected, cleaned, and refitted as needed to serve as spare
units in the event that the City needs to take one of the new units down for cleaning and routine
maintenance. With the current system, the City does not have the flexibility to take a unit offline for
cleaning and maintenance.
Belt Press - The City currently has two belt presses that see heavy use as the demand for biosolids
in compost is high. The two existing presses are 10 years old and are in need of frequent repairs and a
thorough overhaul. The third press will reduce the load on any given press, provide the City greater
flexibility, and give the City some redundancy.
Automatic Control System – The City has included in the Improvement Project a new
Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition ("SCADA") to enable automated control of the new digesters
and all of the sludge management processes. In future projects, SCADA will be included that will, within
a few years, enable complete computer control of the plant and allow real-time monitoring of power,
water, and natural gas utility consumption. The new system uses the same technology as is currently
deployed at the City’s two water treatment facilities (Buckman and Canyon Road). Given that the control
system has been successfully operating at the water treatment facilities, the City expects that utilizing it at
the wastewater treatment facility will give the City better system planning, design, and cross-training.
Cogeneration – The Improvement Project also includes addition of a "combined heat and power"
(chp) component to make use of the biogas generated by the new digesters. The cogeneration will operate
as an integral component of the replacement digesters, enabling the city to make use of the produced
electricity and recovery of heat from the combustion of gas as a source of energy. The cogeneration
design includes gas treatment prior to combustion in either the digester boilers or in the CHP engines,
extending the life of the boilers and simplifying the air emissions permitting of the cogeneration
exhaust. Flaring of digester gas will only be necessary during startup or in the event of equipment
malfunctions. In combination with the present two solar energy systems at the plant, the cogeneration-
produced electricity will supply virtually all of the electric needs of the facility. The city anticipates that7
the new system, which will also be managed by the new computer controls, will allow the plant to
produce over 92% of the electricity on-site (adding to an existing solar power contribution), as well as to
provide over 90% of the required energy for thermal hearing requirements of the digesters. The addition
of cogeneration (power and heat) is a part of an effort to make the city’s wastewater treatment plant more
sustainable to meet the city’s sustainability goals.
CLIMATE BOND CERTIFICATION
Sustainable Santa Fe Sustainability Plan
On November 14, 2018, the governing body of the City adopted a 25 year sustainability plan (the
“Sustainability Plan”), with the established goals of (1) reducing climate impacts through greenhouse gas
reductions and adaptations to achieve carbon neutrality by the year 2040, (2) enhancing environmental
resilience through better management of natural resources, (3) improving economic vitality through
rethinking infrastructure development and other drivers of economic development, and (4) enhancing
quality of life for all citizens of the City by embedding social equity and access to factors for success into
sustainability strategies (more information regarding the Sustainability Plan is available on the City’s
website at https://www.santafenm.gov/sustainable_santa_fe ). In furtherance of the objectives of the
Sustainability Plan, the Improvement Project financed by the 2019 Bonds will, in addition to generally
improving the operational and energy efficiencies of the System, allow the System’s treatment facility to
achieve net-zero electricity consumption. In furtherance of the promotion of the Sustainability Plan, the
2019 Bonds will be identified as “Climate Bond Certified” based on the Climate Bond Certification
(defined below) as further set forth below. The City is the first issuer in New Mexico to obtain Climate
Bond Certification. Additionally, CBI has indicated that the portion of the Improvement Project related
to the digesters is the first stand-alone anaerobic digester project globally to be certified by the Climate
Bonds Initiative.
Climate Bond Certification and Pre-Issuance Process
The information set forth under this caption “CLIMATE BOND CERTIFICATION” concerning
(1) the Climate Bonds Initiative (the “CBI”) and Climate Bond Certification (the “Climate Bond
Certification”), and (2) First Environment, Inc. (the “Verifier”) in its role as verifier with respect to the
Climate Bond Certification, all as more fully described below, has been extracted from materials
provided by the CBI and the Verifier, respectively, for such purposes, and none of such information is
guaranteed as to accuracy or completeness or is to be construed as a representation by the City or the
Underwriters. Additional information relating to the CBI, the Climate Bond Certification, and the
process for obtaining Climate Bond Certification can be found at www.climatebonds.net. This hyperlink
is included solely for the reader’s convenience and such website link and the information contained
therein is not incorporated into and is not part of this Official Statement.
The term “Climate Bond Certification” is neither defined in, nor related to, the Ordinance and
the use of such terms herein is for identification purposes only and is not intended to provide or imply
that a Beneficial Owner of the 2019 Bonds is entitled to any additional security other than as provided in
the Ordinance (see “SECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT FOR THE 2019 BONDS”) . The
Climate Bond Certification and the identification of the 2019 Bonds as Climate Certified Bonds does not
affect the underlying security for the payment of the 2019 Bonds. The repayment obligations of the City
with respect to the 2019 Bonds are not conditioned upon CBI’s certification or continuing certification of
the 2019 Bonds by the CBI.8
As a component of the City’s Sustainability Plan, the City applied for certification of the 2019
Bonds to the Climate Bonds Standard Board of the Climate Bonds Initiative (the “CBI”), an international
non-profit organization that promotes investments in projects to produce a low carbon and climate
resilient economy. The City received certification of the 2019 Bonds as “Certified Climate Bonds.” The
purpose of designating the 2019 Bonds as “Certified Climate Bonds / Green Bonds” is to allow investors
to invest directly in bonds that finance environmentally beneficial projects. See “THE IMPROVEMENT
PROJECT” herein.
A climate bond is used to finance projects which have features that will address climate change
issues. Certification of a bond as a Climate Bond means that the bonds meet the requirements of the
Climate Bonds Standard established by the Climate Bonds Standard Board of CBI as verified by an
independent third-party verification agent. As a part of the certification process, the City retained the
Verifier to provide a third-party verification that the 2019 Bonds meet the Climate Bonds Standard. All
of the projects included in the Improvement Project have been certified under the Climate Bonds Standard
Water Sector Criteria. The certification of the 2019 Bonds reflects only the views of the Verifier report
approved by the Climate Bonds Standard Board.
The requirements of the Certification Process include pre-issuance requirements, which must be
met by issuers seeking certification ahead of issuance, and post-issuance requirements, which must be met
by issuers seeking continued certification following the issuance of bonds. The pre-issuance requirements
are designed to ensure that the City has established appropriate internal processes and controls prior to
issuance of the Bonds, and that such internal processes and controls are sufficient to enable conformance
with the Certification Process following the issuance of bonds and in connection with the expenditure of
bond proceeds.
Water Standards
The Improvement Project has been certified as meeting the criteria for Climate Bonds Standard’s
water eligible project category based on the expectation that the Improvement Project will meet the
requirements of the Mitigation component (promoting greenhouse gas mitigation through reduced
emissions or increased carbon sequestration) and Adaptation and Resilience component (promoting
adaptation to climate change and facilitating increased climate resilience in the systems in which they are
located). To meet the Mitigation component, the Improvement Project must either have (i) no expected
net greenhouse gas emissions impact or (ii) a negative net greenhouse gas emissions impact through
either decreased emissions or increased sequestration relative to a business as usual baseline. To meet the
Adaptation and Resilience component a project must have an expected or remaining operational life of
more than 20 years. Additionally, for the Adaptation and Resilience analysis, a vulnerability assessment
(an assessment of climate impacts and potential climate risks) and an adaptation plan (management’s
response to the conclusions and findings in the vulnerability assessment addressing how the identified
climate risks will be addressed) are evaluated for climate vulnerability and aspects of governance and
conflict negotiations between water users in shifting hydrological conditions along with components of
technical diagnostics and nature-based solutions.
Post Issuance Reporting
The requirements of the Climate Bonds Standard include post-issuance requirements which need
to be met by the City for continued certification following the issuance of the 2019 Bonds. To maintain
the certification of the 2019 Bonds as Certified Climate Bonds, the City is required to engage the Verifier
once within 12 months of the issuance of the 2019 Bonds to confirm that the 2019 Bonds conform with
the requirements of the Climate Bonds Standard; beyond the one-time, post-issuance verification, no
further verification is required, and the City does not intend to conduct further verification. Under its9
agreement with CBI to maintain the climate bonds designation, the City has agreed to (1) provide CBI, no
later than 120 days following the end of its fiscal year, an annual statement certifying conformance with
the Climate Bond Standard, and (2) provide holders of the 2019 Bonds a generalized annual update on the
Improvement Project within 120 days of the end of each fiscal year. The City expects to post the annual
updates to 2019 Bondholders on EMMA.
The CBI is not a licensed broker-dealer or a nationally recognized statistical ratings organization
and the Climate Bond Certification by the CBI is not a recommendation to buy, sell or hold securities.
No assurance can be given as to the outcome of the post issuance assessments by the Verifier. CBI’s
certification may be subject to revision or withdrawal, including, without limitation, in the event that the
City’s future capital expenditures from the proceeds of the 2019 Bonds vary from the anticipated
expenditures reviewed by the CBI. The City will undertake reasonable efforts to ensure that any
adjustment of capital expenditures of the 2019 Bond proceeds or other actions taken with respect to the
2019 Bonds will not result in revision or withdrawal of the CBI’s certification; however, there can be no
assurance that such adjustment or other action or a future revision to the CBI’s criteria for certifying
bonds will not result in a withdrawal or revision of the CBI’s certification. Failure of the City to provide
either its annual statement to CBI or such annual update could result in revocation of the Climate Bond
Certification. While the City intends to continue to provide such statement and report, the holders of the
2019 Bonds have no right to enforce the provisions of such agreement and the City has no obligation to
maintain the certification of the 2019 Bonds as Climate Certified Bonds and assumes no obligation to
ensure compliance with any legal or other principles of Climate Bonds as such principles may evolve over
time.
Limited Purpose of Climate Bond Certification
The certification of the 2019 Bonds as “Climate Bonds” by the CBI is based solely on the
Climate Bonds Standard and does not, and is not intended to make any representation or give any
assurance with respect to any other matter relating to the 2019 Bonds or any part of the Improvement
Project, including but not limited to this Official Statement, the Ordinance, the City or the management of
the City.
The certification of the 2019 Bonds by the CBI was addressed solely to the City and is not a
recommendation to any person to purchase, hold or sell the 2019 Bonds and such certification does not
address the market price or suitability of the 2019 Bonds for a particular investor. The certification also
does not address the merits of the decision by the City or any third party to participate in the Improvement
Project and does not express and should not be deemed to be an expression of an opinion as to the City or
any aspect of the Improvement Project (including but not limited to the financial viability of any part of
the Improvement Project) other than with respect to the conformance with the Climate Bonds Standard.
In issuing or monitoring, as applicable, the certification, the CBI has assumed and relied upon and
will assume and rely upon the accuracy and completeness in all material respects of the information
supplied or otherwise made available to the CBI. The CBI does not assume or accept any responsibility
to any person for independently verifying (and has not verified) such information or to undertake (and has
not undertaken) any independent evaluation of the Improvement Project or the City. In addition, the CBI
does not assume any obligation to conduct (and it has not conducted) any physical inspection of the
Improvement Project. The certification may only be used with the 2019 Bonds and may not be used for
any other purpose without the CBI’s prior written consent.
The certification does not and is not in any way intended to address the likelihood of timely
payment of interest when due on the 2019 Bonds and or the payment of principal at maturity or any other
date.10
The certification may be withdrawn at any time in the CBI’s sole and absolute discretion and
there can be assurance that such certification will not be withdrawn.
BAM GREENSTAR BONDS
The 2019 Bonds have been designated BAM GreenStar Bonds because BAM has determined that
the use of bond proceeds by the City as described in this Official Statement and in any additional
information obtained by BAM aligns with one of the Green Bond Principals (GBPs) developed by the
International Capital Markets Association (ICMA). The GBPs were developed by the ICMA with the
goal of establishing universally accepted guidelines for the issuance of green bonds, and one of the key
requirements addresses the use of proceeds. BAM has been identified by the ICMA as an observer
organization that is active in the field of green and/or social or sustainability finance and is Climate Bond
Initiative approved verifier. The Credit Profile prepared by BAM for the 2019 Bonds will identify which
of the following GBP categories applies to the 2019 Bonds:
 renewable energy
 energy efficiency
 pollution prevention and control
 environmentally sustainable management of living natural resources and land use
 terrestrial and aquatic biodiversity
 clean transportation
 climate change adaptation
 sustainable water and wastewater management
 green buildings.
Each of the GBPs correlates to one of the following UN Sustainable Development Goals which
will also be included in the Credit Profile for the 2019 Bonds:
 clean water and sanitation
 affordable and clean energy
 sustainable cities and communities
 industry innovation and infrastructure
 responsible consumption and production
 climate action
 life below water11

DESCRIPTION OF THE 2019 BONDS
General
The 2019 Bonds are being issued in the aggregate principal amount of $13,550,000 in order to
provide funds for the Improvement Project. See “THE IMPROVEMENT PROJECT.”
The 2019 Bonds will be dated their date of issuance and delivery. The 2019 Bonds will bear
interest at the rates, and will mature in the amounts and on the dates set forth on the inside front cover
page of this Official Statement. Interest on the 2019 Bonds will be payable semiannually on June 1 and
December 1 of each year, commencing June 1, 2019. The 2019 Bonds will bear interest from their date
of issuance and delivery. Interest on the 2019 Bonds will be computed on the basis of a 360-day year
consisting of twelve 30-day months. The 2019 Bonds will be issued as fully registered bonds in
denominations of $5,000 or any integral multiple thereof; provided that no 2019 Bonds may be in a
denomination which exceeds the principal coming due on any maturity date, and no individual 2019 Bond
will be issued for more than one maturity.
The principal of any 2019 Bond will be payable to the registered owner thereof as shown on the
registration books with respect to the 2019 Bonds kept by BOKF, NA, as registrar (the “Registrar”), upon
maturity or prior redemption thereof and upon presentation and surrender to BOKF, NA, as paying agent
(the “Paying Agent”). If any 2019 Bond is not paid upon such presentation and surrender at or after
maturity or on a designated prior redemption date on which the City may have exercised its right to
redeem prior to maturity any 2019 Bond, it will continue to draw interest at the rate borne by the 201913
Bond until the principal thereof is paid in full. Payment of interest on any 2019 Bond will be made by
check or draft mailed by the Paying Agent, on or before each interest payment date (or, if such interest
payment date is not a business day, on or before the next succeeding business day), to the registered
owner thereof as of the fifteenth day of the calendar month (whether or not a business day) preceding
each regularly scheduled interest payment date on the 2019 Bonds (the “Regular Record Date”) at the
address as it last appears on the registration books with respect to the 2019 Bonds on the Regular Record
Date (or by such other arrangements as may be mutually agreed to by the Paying Agent and any
registered owner on such Regular Record Date) notwithstanding any transfer or exchange thereof
subsequent to such Regular Record Date and prior to such interest payment date. Any interest not so
timely paid or duly provided for will cease to be payable as described above and will be payable to the
person in whose name any 2019 Bond is registered at the close of business on a special record date to be
fixed by the Registrar (the “Special Record Date”) whenever moneys become available for payment of
any such defaulted interest. Notice of the Special Record Date will be given not less than 10 days prior
thereto, by first-class mail, to the registered owners of the 2019 Bonds. See “—Book-Entry Only
System.”
All payments of principal and interest on the 2019 Bonds will be made in lawful money of the
United States of America. The City and the Registrar may treat the registered owner of a 2019 Bond as
the absolute owner thereof for all purposes except as otherwise provided in the Bond Ordinance with
respect to the Regular Record Date and the Special Record Date for the payment of interest. Payment of
or on account of either principal or redemption price or interest on any 2019 Bond will be made only to or
upon the written order of the registered owner thereof or his legal representative. All such payments will
be valid and effectual to discharge the liability upon the 2019 Bond to the extent of the sum or sums so
paid.
Redemption of 2019 Bonds
Optional Redemption . The 2019 Bonds maturing on or after June 1, 2029, are subject to
redemption prior to maturity at the option of the City in one or more units of principal of $5,000 on and
after June 1, 2028, in whole or in part at any time, in such order of maturities as the City may determine
(and by lot if less than all 2019 Bonds of such maturity is called, such selection by lot to be made by the
Registrar in such manner as it considers appropriate and fair) at a redemption price equal to the principal
amount of the 2019 Bonds or portions thereof to be redeemed, plus accrued interest thereon to the
redemption date, without premium.
Redemption Procedures . At least 60 days prior to any date selected by the City for optional
redemption of any of the 2019 Bonds, the City shall give written instructions to the Registrar with respect
to the optional redemption. The Registrar shall not be required to give notice of any optional redemption
unless the Registrar has received written instructions from the City in regard thereto at least 60 days prior
to such redemption date (unless such deadline is waived by the Registrar). Additionally, notice of
optional redemption shall be given by the City by sending a copy of such notice by first-class, postage
prepaid mail, not less than thirty days prior to the optional redemption date to the Paying Agent, if the
Registrar is not the Paying Agent.
Notice of redemption of 2019 Bonds will be given by the Registrar by sending a copy of such
notice in the manner required by the Depository or by first-class, postage prepaid mail not more than 60
and not less than 30 days prior to the redemption date to each registered owner of each 2019 Bond
selected for redemption as shown on the registration books kept by the Registrar as of the date of mailing
of notice. Failure to give such notice by mailing to the registered owner of any 2019 Bond, or any defect
therein, or the failure of any depository to notify any of its participants of the failure of any such14
participant or an indirect participant to notify a beneficial owner of any such redemption, will not affect
the validity of the proceedings for the redemption of any of the 2019 Bonds.
The notice shall specify the number or numbers of the 2019 Bond or 2019 Bonds or portions
thereof to be so redeemed (if less than all are to be redeemed); and all notices shall specify the date fixed
for redemption, and shall further state that on such redemption date there will become and be due and
payable upon each $5,000 unit of principal so to be redeemed at the Paying Agent the principal thereof,
accrued interest, if any, to the redemption date, and the applicable prior redemption premium thereon (if
any), and that from and after such date interest will cease to accrue. Accrued interest to the redemption
date will be paid by check or draft mailed to the registered owner (or by alterative means if so agreed to
by the Paying Agent and the registered owner). Notice having been given in the manner hereinbefore
provided, the Bond or Bonds so called for redemption shall become due and payable on the redemption
date so designated; and upon presentation thereof at the Paying Agent, the City will pay the Bond or
Bonds so called for redemption and the applicable prior redemption premium (if any). In the event that
only a portion of the principal amount of a Bond is so redeemed, a new Bond representing the
unredeemed principal shall be duly completed, authenticated and delivered by the Registrar to the
registered owner pursuant to the Bond Ordinance and without charge to the registered owner thereof. The
Registrar and Paying Agent shall comply with any other terms regarding redemption and notice of
redemption as required by any applicable agreement with a Depository.
If money or Government Obligations sufficient to pay the redemption price of the 2019 Bonds to
be called for redemption are not on deposit with the Paying Agent prior to the giving of notice of
redemption, such notice will state such 2019 Bonds will be redeemed in whole or in part on the
redemption date in a principal amount equal to that part of the redemption price received by the Paying
Agent on the applicable redemption date. If the full amount of the redemption price is not received as set
forth in the preceding sentence, the notice will be effective only for those 2019 Bonds for which the
redemption price is on deposit with the Paying Agent. If all 2019 Bonds called for redemption cannot be
redeemed, the 2019 Bonds to be redeemed will be selected in a manner deemed reasonable and fair by the
City and the Registrar will give notice, in the manner in which the original notice of redemption was
given, that such money was not received and the information required by the preceding paragraph. In that
event, the Registrar will promptly return to the registered owners thereof the 2019 Bonds or certificates
which it has received evidencing the part thereof which have not been redeemed.
Registration, Transfer and Exchange of 2019 Bonds
Books for the registration and transfer of the 2019 Bonds shall be kept by the Registrar. Upon the
surrender for transfer of any 2019 Bonds at the Registrar, duly endorsed for transfer or accompanied by
an assignment duly executed by the registered owner or his attorney duly authorized in writing, the
Registrar shall authenticate and deliver in the name of the transferee or transferees a new 2019 Bond or
Bonds of a like aggregate principal amount and of the same maturity, bearing a number or numbers not
contemporaneously outstanding. 2019 Bonds may be exchanged at the Registrar for an equal aggregate
principal amount of 2019 Bonds of the same maturity of other authorized denominations. The Registrar
shall authenticate and deliver a 2019 Bond or Bonds which the registered owner making the exchange is
entitled to receive, bearing a number or numbers not contemporaneously outstanding. Exchanges and
transfers of 2019 Bonds as provided in the Bond Ordinance shall be without charge to the owner or any
transferee, but the Registrar may require the payment by the owner of any 2019 Bond requesting
exchange or transfer of any tax or other governmental charge required to be paid with respect to such
exchange or transfer.
The Registrar shall not be required (1) to transfer or exchange all or a portion of any 2019 Bond
subject to prior redemption during the period of fifteen days next preceding the mailing of notice to the15
registered owners calling any 2019 Bonds for prior redemption or (2) to transfer or exchange all or a
portion of a 2019 Bond after the mailing to registered owners of notice calling such 2019 Bond or portion
thereof for prior redemption.
If any 2019 Bond is lost, stolen, destroyed or mutilated, the Registrar will, upon receipt of such
evidence, information or indemnity relating thereto as it may reasonably require, authenticate and deliver
a replacement bond or bonds of like aggregate principal amount and of the same subseries and maturity,
bearing a number or numbers not contemporaneously outstanding. If such lost, stolen, destroyed or
mutilated 2019 Bond has matured, the Registrar may direct the Paying Agent to pay such 2019 Bond in
lieu of replacement.
Book-Entry Only System
Introduction
Unless otherwise noted, the information contained under the caption “General” below has been
provided by DTC. Neither the City, the Financial Advisor nor Bond Counsel makes any representations
as to the accuracy or the completeness of such information. The Beneficial Owners of the Bonds should
confirm the following information with DTC, the Direct Participants or the Indirect Participants.
NEITHER THE CITY NOR THE PAYING AGENT WILL HAVE ANY RESPONSIBILITY
OR OBLIGATION TO DIRECT PARTICIPANTS, TO INDIRECT PARTICIPANTS, OR TO ANY
BENEFICIAL OWNER WITH RESPECT TO (A) THE ACCURACY OF ANY RECORDS
MAINTAINED BY DTC, ANY DIRECT PARTICIPANT, OR ANY INDIRECT PARTICIPANT;
(B) ANY NOTICE THAT IS PERMITTED OR REQUIRED TO BE GIVEN TO THE OWNERS OF
THE BONDS UNDER THE BOND LEGISLATION, (C) THE SELECTION BY DTC OR ANY
DIRECT PARTICIPANT OR INDIRECT PARTICIPANT OF ANY PERSON TO RECEIVE
PAYMENT IN THE EVENT OF A PARTIAL REDEMPTION OF THE BONDS; (D) THE PAYMENT
BY DTC OR ANY DIRECT PARTICIPANT OR INDIRECT PARTICIPANT OF ANY AMOUNT
WITH RESPECT TO THE PRINCIPAL OR INTEREST DUE WITH RESPECT TO THE OWNER OF
THE BONDS; (E) ANY CONSENT GIVEN OR OTHER ACTION TAKEN BY DTC AS THE
OWNERS OF THE BONDS; OR (F) ANY OTHER MATTER REGARDING DTC.
General
The Bonds will be issued in book entry form. DTC will act as securities depository for the
Bonds. The Bonds will be issued as fully-registered securities registered in the name of Cede & Co.
(DTC’s partnership nominee) or such other name as may be requested by an authorized representative of
DTC. One fully-registered Bond will be issued for each maturity of the Bonds, each in the aggregate
principal amount of such maturity, and will be deposited with DTC.
DTC, the world’s largest depository, is a limited-purpose trust company organized under the New
York Banking Law, a “banking organization” within the meaning of the New York Banking Law, a
member of the Federal Reserve System, a “clearing corporation” within the meaning of the New York
Uniform Commercial Code, and a “clearing agency” registered pursuant to the provisions of Section 17A
of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934. DTC holds and provides asset servicing for over 3.5 million
issues of U.S. and non-U.S. equity issues, corporate and municipal debt issues, and money market
instruments (from over 100 countries) that DTC’s participants (“Direct Participants”) deposit with DTC.
DTC also facilitates the post-trade settlement among Direct Participants of sales and other securities
transactions in deposited securities, through electronic computerized book-entry transfers and pledges
between Direct Participants’ accounts. This eliminates the need for physical movement of securities16
certificates. Direct Participants include both U.S. and non-U.S. securities brokers and dealers, banks,
trust companies, clearing corporations, and certain other organizations. DTC is a wholly-owned
subsidiary of The Depository Trust & Clearing Corporation (“DTCC”). DTCC is the holding company for
DTC, National Securities Clearing Corporation, and Fixed Income Clearing Corporation, all of which are
registered clearing agencies. DTCC is owned by the users of its regulated subsidiaries. Access to the
DTC system is also available to others such as both U.S. and non-U.S. securities brokers and dealers,
banks, trust companies, and clearing corporations that clear through or maintain a custodial relationship
with a Direct Participant, either directly or indirectly (“Indirect Participants”). DTC has a Standard &
Poor’s rating of AA+. The DTC Rules applicable to Direct Participants are on file with the Securities and
Exchange Commission. More information about DTC can be found at www.dtcc.com. The City
undertakes no responsibility for and makes no representations as to the accuracy or the completeness of
the content of such material contained on that website as described in the preceding sentence, including,
but not limited to, updates of such information or links to other Internet sites accessed through the
aforementioned website.
Purchases of the Bonds under the DTC system must be made by or through Direct or Indirect
Participants, which will receive a credit for the Bonds on DTC’s records. The ownership interest of each
actual purchaser of each Bond (“Beneficial Owner”) is in turn to be recorded on the Direct and Indirect
Participants’ records. Beneficial Owners will not receive written confirmation from DTC of their
purchase. Beneficial Owners are, however, expected to receive written confirmations providing details of
the transaction, as well as periodic statements of their holdings, from the Direct or Indirect Participant
through which the Beneficial Owner entered into the transaction. Transfers of ownership interests in the
Bonds are to be accomplished by entries made on the books of Direct and Indirect Participants acting on
behalf of Beneficial Owners. Beneficial Owners will not receive certificates representing their ownership
interests in the Bonds, except in the event that use of the book-entry system for the Bonds is discontinued.
To facilitate subsequent transfers, all Bonds deposited by Direct Participants with DTC are
registered in the name of DTC’s partnership nominee, Cede & Co., or such other name as may be
requested by an authorized representative of DTC. The deposit of Bonds with DTC and their registration
in the name of Cede & Co. or such other DTC nominee do not affect any change in beneficial ownership.
DTC has no knowledge of the actual Beneficial Owners of the Bonds; DTC’s records reflect only the
identity of the Direct Participants to whose accounts such Bonds are credited, which may or may not be
the Beneficial Owners. The Direct and Indirect Participants will remain responsible for keeping account
of their holdings on behalf of their customers.
Conveyance of notices and other communications by DTC to Direct Participants, by Direct
Participants to Indirect Participants, and by Direct Participants and Indirect Participants to Beneficial
Owners will be governed by arrangements among them, subject to any statutory or regulatory
requirements as may be in effect from time to time.
Redemption notices will be sent to DTC. If less than all of the Bonds are being redeemed, DTC’s
practice is to determine by lot the amount of the interest of each Direct Participant in such issue to be
redeemed.
Neither DTC nor Cede & Co. (nor any other DTC nominee) will consent or vote with respect to
the Bonds unless authorized by a Direct Participant in accordance with DTC’s procedures. Under its
usual procedures, DTC will mail an Omnibus Proxy to the City as soon as possible after the record date.
The Omnibus Proxy assigns Cede & Co.’s consenting or voting rights to those Direct Participants to
whose accounts the Bonds are credited on the record date (identified in a listing attached to the Omnibus
Proxy).17
Principal of and sinking fund and interest payments on the Bonds will be made to Cede & Co. or
such other nominee as may be requested by an authorized representative of DTC. DTC’s practice is to
credit Direct Participants’ accounts, on each payable date in accordance with their respective holdings
shown on DTC’s records unless DTC has reason to believe that it will not receive payment on the date
payable. Payments by Participants to Beneficial Owners will be governed by standing instructions and
customary practices, as is the case with securities held for the accounts of customers in bearer form or
registered in “street name,” and will be the responsibility of such Participant and not of DTC, agent, or
the City, subject to any statutory or regulatory requirements as may be in effect from time to time.
Payment of principal and interest to Cede & Co. (or such other nominee as may be requested by an
authorized representative of DTC) is the responsibility of the City or agent, disbursement of such
payments to Direct Participants shall be the responsibility of DTC or the Paying Agent, and disbursement
of such payments to the Beneficial Owners shall be the responsibility of Direct and Indirect Participants.
DTC may discontinue providing its services as securities depository with respect to the Bonds at
any time by giving reasonable notice to the City. Under such circumstances, in the event that a successor
securities depository is not obtained, security certificates are required to be printed and delivered as
described in the bond legislation.
The City may decide to discontinue use of the system of book-entry transfers through DTC (or a
successor securities depository). In that event, the Bonds will be printed and delivered as described in the
bond legislation.
The City cannot and does not give any assurances that DTC will distribute to Participants, or that
Participants or others will distribute to the Beneficial Owners, payments of principal of and interest and
premium, if any, on the Bonds paid or any redemption or other notices or that they will do so on a timely
basis or will serve and act in the manner described in this Official Statement. The City is not responsible
or liable for the failure of DTC or any Direct Participant or Indirect Participant to make any payments or
give any notice to a Beneficial Owner with respect to the Bonds or any error or delay relating thereto.
The foregoing description of the procedures and record keeping with respect to beneficial
ownership interests in the Bonds, payment of principal of and interest and other payments with respect to
the Bonds to Direct Participants, Indirect Participants or Beneficial Owners, confirmation and transfer of
beneficial ownership interest in such Bonds and other related transactions by and between DTC, the
Direct Participants, the Indirect Participants and the Beneficial Owners is based solely on information
provided by DTC. Accordingly, no representations can be made concerning these matters and neither the
Direct Participants, the Indirect Participants nor the Beneficial Owners should rely on the foregoing
information with respect to such matters but should instead confirm the same with DTC or the
Participants, as the case may be.
SO LONG AS CEDE & CO. IS THE REGISTERED OWNER OF THE BONDS, AS NOMINEE
OF DTC, REFERENCES HEREIN TO THE HOLDERS SHALL MEAN CEDE & CO., AS
AFORESAID, AND SHALL NOT MEAN THE BENEFICIAL OWNERS OF THE BONDS.

SECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT FOR THE 2019 BONDS
Limited Obligations
The 2019 Bonds are limited obligations of the City and are payable as to principal and interest
exclusively from the Pledged Revenues. The Pledged Revenues consist of: (a) the Environmental
Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues including the gross receipts tax distribution to the City made
pursuant to Section 7-1-6.46, NMSA, which represents the amount of Environmental Services Gross
Receipts Tax Revenues that would have been remitted to the City but for the deductions provided by
Sections 7-9-92 and 7-9-93, NMSA, and any similar distributions made to the City in lieu of
Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues pursuant to law (see “SPECIAL FACTORS
RELATING TO THE 2019 BONDS—Legislative Changes”) and (b) the Wastewater System Net
Revenues (collectively the “Pledged Revenues”). For further information concerning these revenues, see
“THE WASTEWATER UTILITY SYSTEM” and “INFORMATION CONCERNING
ENVIRONMENTAL SERVICES GROSS RECEIPTS TAXES AND REVENUES” herein.
Additionally, there are pledged to secure the payment of the principal and interest on the 2019 Bonds in
accordance with their terms certain amounts held under the Bond Ordinance (except for amounts held in
the Rebate Fund), subject only to the provisions of the Bond Ordinance permitting the application thereof
for the purposes and on the terms and conditions set forth therein.
THE 2019 BONDS DO NOT CONSTITUTE AN INDEBTEDNESS OF THE CITY WITHIN
THE MEANING OF ANY CONSTITUTIONAL, CHARTER OR STATUTORY PROVISION OR
LIMITATION, NOR WILL THEY BE CONSIDERED OR HELD TO BE GENERAL OBLIGATIONS
OF THE CITY. NEITHER THE FULL FAITH AND CREDIT NOR THE TAXING POWER OF THE
CITY, THE STATE OR ANY POLITICAL SUBDIVISION OR PUBLIC AGENCY THEREOF,
OTHER THAN THE CITY TO THE EXTENT OF THE PLEDGED REVENUES THAT ARE
PLEDGED TO THE PAYMENT OF THE PRINCIPAL OF AND INTEREST ON THE 2019 BONDS.
NO OWNER HAS THE RIGHT TO COMPEL THE EXERCISE OF THE TAXING POWER OF THE
CITY OR THE FORFEITURE OF ANY OF ITS PROPERTY IN CONNECTION WITH ANY
DEFAULT UNDER THE BOND ORDINANCE.
The Net Revenues will be received and held by the City for the benefit of the owners of the
2012B Bonds, the 2019 Bonds, and any other Parity Obligations; and the Environmental Services Gross
Receipts Tax Revenues will be received and held by the City for the benefit of the owners of the 2012B
Bonds, the 2019 Bonds, and any other Parity EGRT Obligations or Superior Tax Obligations. The
Pledged Revenues will be disbursed, allocated and applied solely for the uses and purposes described
below under “SUMMARY OF CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF THE BOND ORDINANCE—
Administration of Wastewater Fund and Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenue Funds.”
Amounts on deposit in each of the funds and accounts established pursuant to the Bond Ordinance will be
invested in Permitted Investments. Investment income on amounts in any fund or account will be
credited to such fund or account, and any loss will be charged to such fund or account.
Pledged Net Revenues
All Net Revenues are irrevocably pledged by the City to secure the punctual payment of the
principal of, redemption premium, if any, and interest on the 2019 Bonds and any other Parity Obligations
in accordance with their terms, and the Net Revenues will not be used for any other purpose while any of
the 2019 Bonds remain Outstanding except as permitted by the provisions of the Bond Ordinance.
The pledge of the Net Revenues will constitute a first lien (but not necessarily an exclusive first
lien) on the Net Revenues on parity thereon with the lien of any Parity Obligations. Such pledge of the19
Net Revenues and the pledge of the amounts in funds created under the Bond Ordinance will be valid and
binding from and after the delivery of the 2019 Bonds without any physical delivery thereof or further act.
The Net Revenues pledged to the payment of the 2019 Bonds and any other Parity Obligations will be
applied to the 2019 Bonds and any other Parity Obligations, without priority or distinction of one over the
other. Other than the 2012B Bonds and the 2019 Bonds, the Net Revenues are not pledged to the
payment of any other outstanding Obligations of the City.
Pledged Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues
All Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues are irrevocably pledged by the City to
secure the punctual payment of the principal of, redemption premium, if any, and interest on the 2012B
Bonds, the 2019 Bonds and any other Parity Obligations or Superior Tax Obligations in accordance with
their terms, and the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues will not be used for any other
purpose while any of the 2019 Bonds remain outstanding except as permitted by the provisions of the
Bond Ordinance. After all payments of debt service and other obligations associated with any
outstanding Superior Tax Obligations are made, the remaining Environmental Services Gross Receipts
Tax Revenues, if any, will be used to pay the 2012B Bonds, the 2019 Bonds and any other Parity
Obligations.
The pledge of the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues will constitute a
subordinate lien (but not necessarily an exclusive subordinate lien) on the Environmental Services Gross
Receipts Tax Revenues on parity thereon with the lien of the 2012B Bonds. Obligations issued with a
superior lien on the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues may only be issued as Superior
Tax Obligations, i.e. as Obligations secured by Additional Gross Receipts Tax Revenues. There are
currently no outstanding Superior Tax Obligations. Such pledge of the Environmental Services Gross
Receipts Tax Revenues and the pledge of the amounts in funds created under the Bond Ordinance will be
valid and binding from and after the delivery of the 2019 Bonds without any physical delivery thereof or
further act.
The Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues pledged to the payment of the 2019
Bonds and any other Parity Obligations will be applied to the 2019 Bonds and the other Parity EGRT
Obligations, without priority or distinction of one over the other, after payment of any outstanding
Superior Tax Obligations. Out of the remaining Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues
there will be applied all sums required for the payment of the principal of, redemption premium, if any,
and interest on the 2019 Bonds (to the extent that all required payments have not been made from
Wastewater System Net Revenues) and any other Parity EGRT Obligations. Remaining Environmental
Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues, after making the foregoing allocations, will be available to the
City for all lawful City purposes. The pledge of the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax
Revenues to the 2019 Bonds will be irrevocable until all 2019 Bonds are no longer outstanding.
Reserve Fund – Municipal Bond Debt Service Reserve Insurance Policy
Concurrently with the issuance of the Bonds, the City will deposit a Reserve Fund Insurance
Policy (the “Reserve Policy”) issued by Build America Mutual Assurance Company (“BAM”) in an
amount equal to the Reserve Requirement, into the Reserve Fund. The Reserve Policy in the Reserve
Fund shall be maintained by the City and used for debt service for the 2019 Bonds upon a deficiency in
Pledged Revenues.20
INFORMATION CONCERNING ENVIRONMENTAL SERVICES GROSS RECEIPTS TAX
AND REVENUES
Authority for Imposition of the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax . Section 7-19D-10,
NMSA, authorizes municipalities to impose by ordinance an excise tax, known as an environmental
services gross receipts tax, equal to 0.0625% of the gross receipts of any person engaging in business in
the municipality. An election of the registered electors of a municipality is not required unless the
municipality chooses to submit the ordinance to its registered electors. The ordinance imposing or
amending an environmental services gross receipts tax becomes effective either July 1 or January 1,
whichever date occurs first after the expiration of three months from the date the ordinance is mailed or
delivered to the Department. No referendum election was held for the City’s Environmental Services
Gross Receipts Tax described below.
Description of the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Imposed by the City . The City
adopted Ordinance No. 1993-20, effective January 1, 1994, which imposed upon persons engaging in
business in the City, for the privilege of engaging in such business, an environmental services gross
receipts tax equal to 0.0625% of the gross receipts reported or required to be reported pursuant to the
Gross Receipts and Compensating Tax Act (the “Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax”).
Ordinance No. 1993-20 dedicates the proceeds of the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax to the
acquisition, construction, operation and maintenance of solid waste facilities, water facilities, wastewater
facilities, sewer systems and related facilities. The revenues received from the Environmental Services
Gross Receipts Tax have been pledged to the payment of the 2012B Bonds.
Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues Report. Set forth in the following table is a
10-year history of the Environmental Services Gross Receipts Tax Revenues received by the City.
